# !filesay | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!filesay` command allows streamers and moderators to execute multiple commands or messages stored in a text file hosted at a public URL. Each line in the text file is sent as a separate command/message to the chat. This is extremely useful for performing bulk actions, such as banning multiple users listed in a file.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#usage "Direct link to Usage")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To execute the commands/messages from a file URL:

    !filesay <url>

**Important:**

*   By default, only users with **Super Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.
*   The URL must point to a **raw text file** (e.g., a Pastebin raw link, a GitHub raw file link).
*   Each line in the file will be executed as if typed directly into chat. Ensure the commands are valid (e.g., `!ban username`).
*   There might be rate limits on how many lines can be processed quickly.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Example File (`https://pastebin.com/raw/examplebans`):**

    /ban BotUser1 Spamming/ban TrollAccount2 Being disruptive/timeout AnotherUser 600 Repeat offences

**Using the command:**

example chat

![broadcaster badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/5527c58c-fb7d-422d-b71b-f309dcb85cc1/3 "broadcaster")BroadcasterName:!filesay https://pastebin.com/raw/examplebans

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:Executing 3 lines from URL...

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:BotUser1 has been permanently banned from the chat.

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:TrollAccount2 has been permanently banned from the chat.

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:AnotherUser has been timed out for 600 seconds.

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<url>` (Required): The direct URL to a plain text file where each line contains a command or message to be sent.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   No specific module needs to be enabled, but the command relies on the bot having the necessary permissions to execute the commands listed within the file (e.g., ban permissions).
*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!nuke`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke)
    : Times out all users who recently chatted based on a specific phrase.
*   [`!nukeusername`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername)
    : Times out all users whose usernames match a pattern.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are no aliases for the `!filesay` command.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#parameters)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#related-commands)
    
*   [Aliases](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay#aliases)

# $(bttvemotes) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(bttvemotes)` variable lists all active BetterTTV (BTTV) emotes in your Twitch channel. This feature allows streamers and viewers to easily see which custom BTTV emotes are available for use in the chat.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use this variable, simply include `$(bttvemotes)` in your chatbot command or message. The variable doesn't require any additional parameters.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Example 1: Displaying BTTV Emotes[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#example-1-displaying-bttv-emotes "Direct link to Example 1: Displaying BTTV Emotes")

**Command:**

    !bttvemotes

**Chatbot Response:**

    The active BTTV emotes in this channel are: $(bttvemotes)

**Output:**

    The active BTTV emotes in this channel are: LULW KEKW 5Head PogU

### Example 2: Creating a Custom Command[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#example-2-creating-a-custom-command "Direct link to Example 2: Creating a Custom Command")

**Command:**

    !command add !customemotes Our channel's BTTV emotes: $(bttvemotes)

**Usage:**

    !customemotes

**Chatbot Response:**

    Our channel's BTTV emotes: LULW KEKW 5Head PogU

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This variable does not accept any parameters.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [$(ffzemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes)
    : Lists active FrankerFaceZ (FFZ) emotes in the channel
*   [$(7tvemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes)
    : Lists active 7TV emotes in the channel

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: How often is the list of BTTV emotes updated?** A: The BTTV emote list is cached for 48 hours. To update the list immediately, you can use the command `!emotes reload`.

**Q: Can I use this variable to check BTTV emotes in other channels?** A: No, the `$(bttvemotes)` variable only shows BTTV emotes for the channel where the chatbot is active.

**Q: What if there are no BTTV emotes enabled in my channel?** A: If no BTTV emotes are enabled, the variable will return an empty result.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#examples)
    *   [Example 1: Displaying BTTV Emotes](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#example-1-displaying-bttv-emotes)
        
    *   [Example 2: Creating a Custom Command](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#example-2-creating-a-custom-command)
        
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#related-commands)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes#faq)

# $(7tvemotes) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#overview "Direct link to Overview")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(7tvemotes)` variable is used to retrieve and display a list of active 7TV emotes in the current Twitch channel. This can be useful for creating commands that inform viewers about available emotes or for integrating emote information into other chatbot functionalities.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#usage "Direct link to Usage")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use this variable, simply include `$(7tvemotes)` in your StreamElements Chatbot command or message. When the command is triggered, the variable will be replaced with a space-separated list of active 7TV emotes.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#examples "Direct link to Examples")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Example 1: Basic Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#example-1-basic-usage "Direct link to Example 1: Basic Usage")

Command:

    !7tvemotes

Chatbot Response:

    The active 7TV emotes in this channel are: $(7tvemotes)

Actual Output:

    The active 7TV emotes in this channel are: LULW KEKW 5Head DinkDonk PogU

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(7tvemotes)` variable does not accept any parameters.

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [$(bttvemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes)
    : Lists active BetterTTV emotes in the channel
*   [$(ffzemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes)
    : Lists active FrankerFaceZ emotes in the channel

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: How often is the 7TV emote list updated?**

A: The 7TV emote list is cached for 48 hours. To update the list immediately, you can use the command `!emotes reload`.

**Q: Can I filter or limit the number of emotes displayed?**

A: The `$(7tvemotes)` variable doesn't have built-in filtering or limiting options. To manipulate the output, you'll need to use additional StreamElements variables or custom code.

**Q: What if there are no 7TV emotes in the channel?**

A: If there are no active 7TV emotes, the variable will return an empty string.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#examples)
    *   [Example 1: Basic Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#example-1-basic-usage)
        
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#related-variables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes#faq)

# $(args) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(args)` variable is a powerful feature in StreamElements chatbot commands that allows you to access and manipulate arguments passed by users. This enables dynamic responses based on user input, enhancing the interactivity of your chatbot.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The basic syntax for using the `$(args)` variable is:

    $(args)

You can access specific arguments using numeric indices, starting from 1:

    $(1), $(2), $(3), etc.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Greeting a user:
    
        Command: !greet $(1)User input: !greet WorldOutput: Hello, World!
    
2.  Introducing a user:
    
        Command: !introduce $(1) is $(2) years oldUser input: !introduce Alice 25Output: Alice is 25 years old
    

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(args)` variable has two special variants:

1.  `$(n.emote)`: Outputs an argument only if it is a valid emote.
    
        Command: !emote $(1.emote)User input: !emote KappaOutput: Kappa
    
2.  `$(n.word)`: Outputs an argument only if it does not contain symbols.
    
        Command: !word $(1.word)User input: !word HelloOutput: Hello
    

Where `n` is the argument index in both cases.

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [$(user)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/user)
    : Represents the username of the person using the command
*   [$(channel)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/channel)
    : Represents the channel name where the command is used

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: What happens if I try to access an argument that wasn't provided?**

A: If you try to access an argument that wasn't provided (e.g., `$(2)` when only one argument was given), the output will be blank.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#related-variables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args#faq)

---

# $(getcount) | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(getcount)` variable allows you to retrieve the current value of a counter without incrementing it. This is useful for displaying counter values in chat messages or on stream overlays.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#usage "Direct link to Usage")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(getcount)` variable, you need to provide the name of the counter as a parameter. The syntax is as follows:

    $(getcount counterName)

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here are two practical examples of how to use the `$(getcount)` variable:

1.  Displaying the current number of subscribers:

    We currently have $(getcount subscribers) subscribers! Thank you for your support!

2.  Showing the number of times a specific command has been used:

    The !hug command has been used $(getcount hugs) times in this stream.

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(getcount)` variable takes one parameter:

*   `counterName`: The name of the counter you want to retrieve the value for. This is a required parameter.

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(count)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count)
    : Increments a counter and returns its new value

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Can I use $(getcount) to create a new counter?** A: No, `$(getcount)` only retrieves existing counter values. To create a new counter, use the `$(count)` variable first.

**Q: What happens if I try to get the count of a non-existent counter?** A: If the counter doesn't exist, `$(getcount)` will return 0.

**Q: Is there a limit to how many counters I can have?** A: StreamElements doesn't specify a limit, but it's good practice to use counters judiciously to avoid performance issues.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#related-variables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount#faq)

---

# $(ai) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(ai)` variable allows you to integrate AI into your StreamElements chat commands, generating dynamic responses based on user input. This powerful feature can enhance viewer engagement and create unique interactive experiences in your stream.

warning

The `$(ai)` variable is currently in beta and may be subject to changes.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#usage "Direct link to Usage")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the AI variable, include it in your commands with the following syntax:

    $(ai *your_query_here*)

Replace `*your_query_here*` with the text you want the AI to respond to.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Simple question:
    
        !command add !aihelp ${ai How can I help improve the stream?}
    
2.  Contextual response:
    
        !command add !aifact ${ai You are a knowledgeable historian. Tell me an interesting fact about ${1:}}
    
3.  Roleplaying:
    
        !command add !aipirate ${ai You are a friendly pirate. Greet ${user} and tell them about your latest adventure.}
    
4.  Combining with other variables:
    
        !command add !aiwelcome ${ai Create a warm welcome message for ${1} who was last seen $(user.lastseen ${1}) ago. Their last message was $(user.lastmessage ${1}).}
    

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(ai)` variable accepts a single parameter:

*   `query`: The input text for the AI to generate a response. This parameter is required.

Default Context[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#default-context "Direct link to Default Context")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The AI variable comes with some default context that it's always aware of:

1.  **Channel Emotes**: The AI knows about the custom emotes available in your channel. It can reference and use these emotes in its responses when appropriate.
    
2.  **Sender's Name**: The AI is aware of the name of the user who triggered the command. This allows for personalized responses without explicitly including the user's name in the query.
    
3.  **Current Date**: The AI knows the current date, allowing it to provide timely responses or reference current events when relevant.
    

This default context enables the AI to generate more relevant and personalized responses without requiring you to explicitly include this information in every query.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Ratelimits[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#ratelimits "Direct link to Ratelimits")

To prevent abuse, the `$(ai)` variable has the following rate limits:

| User Type | Requests | Reset Time |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Regular | 3   | 60 seconds |
| Affiliate | 10  | 60 seconds |
| Partner | 30  | 60 seconds |

Best Practices[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#best-practices "Direct link to Best Practices")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Provide clear context in your queries to get more relevant responses.
2.  Use command cooldowns to prevent spam.
3.  Combine the `$(ai)` variable with other StreamElements variables for more dynamic interactions.
4.  Test your AI commands thoroughly before using them in live streams.

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Can I customize the AI's personality?**

A: Yes, you can provide context or instructions in your query to shape the AI's response. For example:

    $(ai You are a friendly pirate. Greet ${user} and share a sea shanty.)

**Q: What happens if I don't provide a query?**

A: If no query is provided, the variable will return an error. Always include a query when using the `$(ai)` variable.

**Q: Can I use the AI variable in combination with other variables?**

A: Yes, you can combine the `$(ai)` variable with other StreamElements variables to create more dynamic and personalized responses. See example 4 in the Examples section.

**Q: Are there any content restrictions for AI-generated responses?**

A: Yes, the AI is programmed to avoid generating inappropriate, offensive, or harmful content. However, it's always a good idea to monitor and moderate AI-generated responses during your stream.

**Q: How long can my query be?**

A: The query limit is 400 characters. For optimal performance, keep your queries concise. If you need a more extensive response, consider breaking it down into multiple separate commands.

**Q: How can I report issues or unexpected behavior with the AI variable?**

A: If you encounter any problems or unexpected responses, you can report them to StreamElements support or post in the official StreamElements Discord for assistance.

Troubleshooting[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#troubleshooting "Direct link to Troubleshooting")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you're experiencing issues with the `$(ai)` variable, try the following:

1.  Check your rate limit usage and wait for the reset if necessary.
2.  Verify that your command syntax is correct.
3.  Ensure that your StreamElements bot has the necessary permissions in your chat.
4.  If problems persist, reach out to StreamElements support for further assistance.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#parameters)
    
*   [Default Context](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#default-context)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#configuration)
    *   [Ratelimits](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#ratelimits)
        
*   [Best Practices](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#best-practices)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#faq)
    
*   [Troubleshooting](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ai#troubleshooting)

# !followage | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!followage` command allows anyone in chat to check how long a specified Twitch user has been following a specified Twitch channel. If no user or channel is specified, it defaults to checking the command user's follow duration for the current channel.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the command with optional parameters:

    !followage [username] [channel_name]

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Check your own follow age:**

example chat

Viewer1:!followage

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Viewer1, You have been following CurrentChannel for 1 year 3 months 5 days 2 hours.

**Check another user's follow age in the current channel:**

example chat

ViewerName:!followage StreamElements

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@User, StreamElements has been following CurrentChannel for 6 years 1 month 10 days 4 hours.

**Check another user's follow age for a different channel:**

example chat

ViewerName:!followage StreamElements AnotherChannel

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@User, StreamElements is not following AnotherChannel.

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `[username]` (Optional): The Twitch username to check the follow age for. Defaults to the user running the command.
*   `[channel_name]` (Optional): The Twitch channel name to check the follow relationship against. Defaults to the current channel where the command is used.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!accountage`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/accountage)
    : Checks when a Twitch account was created.
*   [`!uptime`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/uptime)
    : Shows how long the current stream has been live.
*   [`!watchtime`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/watchtime)
    : Shows how long a user has watched the current channel (requires Loyalty module).

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/followage#related-commands)

# !enablesfx | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!enablesfx` command allows streamers and moderators to quickly re-enable all **sound effect** (SFX) items in the StreamElements loyalty store that were previously disabled (e.g., using `!disablesfx`).

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To enable all SFX store items, use the following command in chat:

    !enablesfx

**Important:** By default, only users with **Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!enablesfx

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, successfully updated 5 items. (SFX store opened)

example chat

![broadcaster badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/5527c58c-fb7d-422d-b71b-f309dcb85cc1/3 "broadcaster")BroadcasterName:!enablesfx

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Broadcaster, No disabled SFX store items found.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The `!enablesfx` command requires the **Stream Store** module to be active and configured with SFX items. Manage this in your **StreamElements Dashboard** under `Loyalty` -> `Stream Store`.
*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!disablesfx`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/disablesfx)
    : Disables all sound effect (SFX) items in the loyalty store.
*   [`!closestore`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/closestore)
    : Disables all _regular_ (non-SFX) items in the loyalty store.
*   [`!openstore`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore)
    : Enables all _regular_ (non-SFX) items in the loyalty store.
*   [`!redeem`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/redeem)
    : Allows viewers to redeem store items.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#examples)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx#related-commands)

# !givepoints | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#overview "Direct link to Overview")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!givepoints` command allows viewers to transfer their loyalty points to another user in the chat. This enables community interactions like gifting points or pooling resources.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To transfer points to another user:

    !givepoints <username> <amount>

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#examples "Direct link to Examples")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

example chat

GenerousViewer:!givepoints LuckyFriend 500

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@GenerousViewer -> gave 500 points to @LuckyFriend

example chat

PoorViewer:!givepoints RichPal 10000

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@PoorViewer, You only have 500 points.

example chat

Viewer:!givepoints NonExistentUser 10

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Viewer, I couldn't find that user in the database :/

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<username>` (Required): The exact username of the recipient.
*   `<amount>` (Required): The number of points to transfer. Must be a positive integer, and the sender must have sufficient points.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The `!givepoints` command requires the **Loyalty system** to be active. Enable it in your **StreamElements Dashboard** under `Loyalty` -> `Loyalty Settings`.
*   The ability for users to give points can be enabled/disabled within the Loyalty Settings.
*   Streamers can set a minimum user level required to use the command and a cooldown period in the command's settings under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!points`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/points)
    : Check your own or another user's point balance.
*   [`!addpoints`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/addpoints)
    : (Moderator+) Manually add points to a user.
*   [`!setpoints`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/setpoints)
    : (Moderator+) Set a user's points to a specific value.
*   [`!top`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/top)
    : View the leaderboard for points.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `!give`
*   `!transfer`

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#parameters)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#related-commands)
    
*   [Aliases](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/givepoints#aliases)

# $(count) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#overview "Direct link to Overview")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(count)` variable is a versatile tool in the StreamElements Chatbot that allows you to create, display, and manipulate custom counters for various purposes in your stream. It's commonly used for tracking deaths in games, counting command usage, or keeping score of any recurring event.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The basic syntax for using the `$(count)` variable is:

    $(count [counter_name] [optional_modifier])

Where:

*   `[counter_name]` is an optional name for your counter (default is the command name)
*   `[optional_modifier]` can be used to set or modify the counter value

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#examples "Direct link to Examples")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Basic usage (increments by 1 each time):
    
        !deaths $(count)
    
2.  Named counter with custom increment:
    
        !bossfails $(count bossfails +1)
    

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `[counter_name]`: (Optional) A unique identifier for your counter. If not specified, the command name is used as the counter name.
*   `[optional_modifier]`: (Optional) Can be used to set or modify the counter value:
    *   `+n`: Increment the counter by n (e.g., `+1`, `+5`)
    *   `-n`: Decrement the counter by n (e.g., `-1`, `-3`)
    *   `n`: Set the counter to a specific value n (e.g., `0`, `100`)

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(getcount)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/getcount)
    : Display the current value of a counter

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Counters are automatically created when first used and persist across stream sessions. You can manage counters in the StreamElements dashboard under the Chatbot section.

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Can I have multiple counters?**

A: Yes, you can create multiple counters by using different names (e.g., `$(count deaths)`, `$(count wins)`).

**Q: How do I reset a counter?** A: You can reset a counter to zero using `$(count [counter_name] 0)`.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#related-variables)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#configuration)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/count#faq)

# $(customapi) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#overview "Direct link to Overview")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(customapi)` variable enables you to make HTTP requests to external APIs and display the responses directly in your stream's chat. This powerful feature allows you to integrate real-time data from various sources into your chat messages and commands.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#usage "Direct link to Usage")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(customapi)` variable, include it in your chat message or command response followed by the URL you want to request:

    $(customapi URL)

Replace _URL_ with the actual API endpoint you want to call.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#examples "Direct link to Examples")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Fetching the latest YouTube video[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#fetching-the-latest-youtube-video "Direct link to Fetching the latest YouTube video")

    $(customapi https://decapi.me/youtube/latest_video?id=UCjerlCIbLPQwSnYlClkjDXg)

Output:

    STREAMELEMENTS PATCH NOTES - SEPTEMBER 10, 2023 #streamelements #updates #patchnotes - https://youtu.be/-q_q37PoaM8

### Getting a random joke[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#getting-a-random-joke "Direct link to Getting a random joke")

    $(customapi https://official-joke-api.appspot.com/random_joke)

Output:

    {"id":323,"type":"general","setup":"Why did the cookie cry?","punchline":"Because his father was a wafer so long!"}

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(customapi)` variable itself doesn't accept parameters. However, you can include query parameters in the URL if the API requires them. For example:

    $(customapi https://api.example.com/data?param1=value1&param2=value2)

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `$(urlfetch)`

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Can I use `$(customapi)` to make POST requests?**

A: No, `$(customapi)` only supports GET requests. Additionally, only HTTP 200 status will return a response. Any other HTTP status will result in a "Unable to make request" response.

**Q: How can I handle JSON responses?**

A: `$(customapi)` returns the raw response. To parse JSON, you may need to use additional tools or custom integrations.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#examples)
    *   [Fetching the latest YouTube video](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#fetching-the-latest-youtube-video)
        
    *   [Getting a random joke](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#getting-a-random-joke)
        
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#parameters)
    
*   [Aliases](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#aliases)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/customapi#faq)

# $(ffzemotes) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#overview "Direct link to Overview")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(ffzemotes)` variable is used to display a list of active FrankerFaceZ (FFZ) emotes in your Twitch channel. This can be helpful for viewers to see which custom emotes are available for use in the chat.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#usage "Direct link to Usage")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use this variable, simply include `$(ffzemotes)` in your chat message or command response. The chatbot will automatically replace it with a list of active FFZ emotes.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#examples "Direct link to Examples")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Example 1: Displaying FFZ Emotes[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#example-1-displaying-ffz-emotes "Direct link to Example 1: Displaying FFZ Emotes")

**Command:**

    !ffzemotes

**Chatbot Response:**

    The active FFZ emotes in this channel are: $(ffzemotes)

**Output:**

    The active FFZ emotes in this channel are: LULW KEKW 5Head PogU

### Example 2: Creating a Custom Command[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#example-2-creating-a-custom-command "Direct link to Example 2: Creating a Custom Command")

**Command:**

    !command add !customemotes Our channel's FFZ emotes: $(ffzemotes)

**Usage:**

    !customemotes

**Chatbot Response:**

    Our channel's FFZ emotes: LULW KEKW 5Head PogU

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This variable does not accept any parameters.

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [$(bttvemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes)
    : Lists active BetterTTV emotes in the channel
*   [$(7tvemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes)
    : Lists active 7TV emotes in the channel

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: How often is the FFZ emote list updated?**

A: The FFZ emote list is cached for 48 hours. To update the list immediately, you can use the command `!emotes reload`.

**Q: Can I filter or limit the number of emotes displayed?**

A: The `$(ffzemotes)` variable doesn't have built-in filtering or limiting options. To manipulate the output, you'll need to use additional StreamElements variables or custom code.

**Q: What if there are no FFZ emotes in the channel?**

A: If there are no active FFZ emotes, the variable will return an empty string.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#examples)
    *   [Example 1: Displaying FFZ Emotes](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#example-1-displaying-ffz-emotes)
        
    *   [Example 2: Creating a Custom Command](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#example-2-creating-a-custom-command)
        
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#related-variables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/ffzemotes#faq)

# $(leagueoflegends) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#overview "Direct link to Overview")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(leagueoflegends)` variable allows you to retrieve and display the current rank and LP (League Points) of a specified League of Legends player using the StreamElements Chatbot.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#usage "Direct link to Usage")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use this variable, you need to provide two parameters: the region and the player's Riot ID or Summoner Name.

    $(leagueoflegends <Riot ID/Summoner Name> <region>)

Riot IDs

League of Legends is transitioning to Riot IDs. During the transition, you can use either Riot IDs or Summoner Names. After the transition, only Riot IDs will be supported.

**Note:** If the Riot ID contains spaces, wrap it in quotes.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#examples "Direct link to Examples")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    $(leagueoflegends styler#euw euw)$(leagueoflegends "Doublelift#na1" na)

Example output:

    Current Rank: Challenger I (1229 LP)

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Region**: The server region of the player (e.g., `euw`, `na`)
2.  **Riot ID/Summoner Name**: The player's unique identifier

Supported Regions[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#supported-regions "Direct link to Supported Regions")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `br` (Brazil)
*   `eune` (Europe Nordic & East)
*   `euw` (Europe West)
*   `jp` (Japan)
*   `kr` (Republic of Korea)
*   `lan` (Latin America North)
*   `las` (Latin America South)
*   `na` (North America)
*   `oce` (Oceania)
*   `pbe` (Public Beta Environment)
*   `ph` (Philippines)
*   `ru` (Russia)
*   `sg` (Singapore)
*   `th` (Thailand)
*   `tw` (Taiwan)
*   `tr` (Turkey)
*   `vn` (Vietnam)

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Why isn't the rank updating immediately?**

A: Rank data may have a slight delay due to API caching. It typically updates within a few minutes after a player's ranked game.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#parameters)
    
*   [Supported Regions](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#supported-regions)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/leagueoflegends#faq)

# $(game) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(game)` variable is a powerful tool that allows you to display the current game being played on a Twitch channel. This variable is particularly useful for creating dynamic commands or messages that reference the streamer's current activity.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(game)` variable, simply include it in your command or message:

    $(game)

You can also check the game of a specific channel by providing a username:

    $(game *username*)

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Display the current game on your channel:
    
        Current game: $(game)
    
    Output: `Current game: Valorant`
    
2.  Check the game on another channel:
    
        $(user) is playing: $(game shroud)
    
    Output: `shroud is playing: Counter-Strike: Global Offensive`
    

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `username` (optional): The Twitch username of the channel you want to check. If not provided, the command will display the game of the current channel.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(title)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title)
    : Displays the current stream title
*   [`$(channel)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/channel)
    : Shows information about the current channel
*   [`$(uptime)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime)
    : Displays how long the current stream has been live

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: How often does the game information update?**

A: The game information typically updates within a few seconds of changing the game on Twitch. However, the exact timing may vary.

**Q: What happens if no game is set?**

A: If no game is set for the channel, the `$(game)` variable will typically return "No game set" or a similar message.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#related-commands)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game#faq)

---

# $(msgid) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#overview "Direct link to Overview")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(msgid)` variable is a powerful tool in the StreamElements Chatbot that outputs the unique message ID of the message that triggered a command. This can be useful for tracking specific messages, debugging, or creating advanced custom functionality in your stream.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(msgid)` variable, simply include it in your command response or custom script. The chatbot will automatically replace it with the actual message ID when the command is triggered.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#examples "Direct link to Examples")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here are two practical examples of how you might use the `$(msgid)` variable:

1.  Basic usage in a command response:

    !messageidBot: The ID of the message that triggered this command is: $(msgid)

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(msgid)` variable does not accept any parameters. It simply returns the message ID of the triggering message.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(user)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/user)
    : Returns the username of the person who triggered the command
*   [`$(channel)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/channel)
    : Returns the name of the channel where the command was triggered

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: What format does the message ID use?**

A: The message ID is typically a UUID (Universally Unique Identifier) in the format of a string of letters and numbers separated by hyphens, such as `bcc9b4bc-566d-4f14-a57d-a86c1c3196f8`.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#related-commands)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/msgid#faq)

---

# !giveaway | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#overview "Direct link to Overview")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!giveaway` command allows anyone in chat to check the status of the currently active channel giveaway. If a giveaway is running, the command provides its name and a direct link for viewers to enter.

**Note:** This command _checks_ the status of an active giveaway. To _start_ or manage giveaways, use the StreamElements Dashboard Giveaway Module.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#usage "Direct link to Usage")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To check the active giveaway details, simply type the command in chat:

    !giveaway

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#examples "Direct link to Examples")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

example chat

ViewerName:!giveaway

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@User, Current giveaway: "Epic New Game Key!" https://streamelements.com/YOUR\_CHANNEL/giveaway/GIVEAWAY\_ID

example chat

ViewerName:!giveaway

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@User, There is currently no giveaway running!

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The `!giveaway` command requires a giveaway to be running. Manage giveaways in your **StreamElements Dashboard** under `Loyalty` -> `Giveaways`.
*   The command response reflects the settings of the currently active giveaway (name, entry requirements) configured by the streamer/moderator.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!ticket`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/ticket)
    : Used by viewers to enter the active giveaway (if it requires loyalty points).
*   [`!raffle`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle)
     / [`!sraffle`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/sraffle)
    : Commands for different types of raffle/giveaway systems.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#examples)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/giveaway#related-commands)

# $(pointsname) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(pointsname)` variable is a dynamic way to display the current name of your stream's loyalty currency in chat messages or commands. It automatically updates to reflect your custom points system name, providing a flexible solution for referencing your loyalty program.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Insert `$(pointsname)` into your chat messages or commands where you want the loyalty currency name to appear. The chatbot will automatically replace it with your actual loyalty points name.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Informing viewers about earning points:

    Earn more $(pointsname) by watching the stream!

Output (assuming your currency is named "memecoins"):

    Earn more memecoins by watching the stream!

2.  Creating a custom command to check points balance:

    !cmd add points Your current $(pointsname) balance is $(user.points).

Output (for a user with 500 points):

    Your current memecoins balance is 500.

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This variable doesn't accept any parameters.

Related Commands/Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#related-commandsvariables "Direct link to Related Commands/Variables")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(user.points)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/user#userpoints)
    : Displays the user's current loyalty points balance
*   [`!addpoints`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/addpoints)
    : Adds points to a user's balance (mod/broadcaster only)
*   [`!setpoints`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/setpoints)
    : Sets a user's points to a specific value (mod/broadcaster only)

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: How do I change my loyalty points name?** A: You can change your loyalty points name in the StreamElements dashboard under the Loyalty tab. The `$(pointsname)` variable will automatically update to reflect the new name.

**Q: Can I use $(pointsname) in custom commands?** A: Yes, you can use `$(pointsname)` in any custom command or chat message where you want to display your loyalty points name.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands/Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#related-commandsvariables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/pointsname#faq)
