# !module | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#overview "Direct link to Overview")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!module` command allows streamers and moderators to enable or disable specific StreamElements chatbot modules directly from the chat. This provides real-time control over features like games, loyalty systems, or other functionalities without needing to access the dashboard.

**Important:** By default, only users with **Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To enable or disable a module:

    !module <module_name> <enable | disable>

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#examples "Direct link to Examples")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Disabling the Roulette game module:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!module roulette disable

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Module Roulette was disabled.

**Enabling the Quotes module:**

example chat

![broadcaster badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/5527c58c-fb7d-422d-b71b-f309dcb85cc1/3 "broadcaster")BroadcasterName:!module quotes enable

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Broadcaster, Module Quotes was enabled.

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<module_name>` (Required): The name of the module to modify (e.g., `roulette`, `duel`, `giveaway`, `quotes`, `loyalty`). Refer to the StreamElements Dashboard (`Chatbot` -> `Modules`) for a list of available module names.
*   `<enable | disable>` (Required): Specify `enable` to turn the module on or `disable` to turn it off.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Available modules and their current status can be viewed in the **StreamElements Dashboard** under `Chatbot` -> `Modules`.
*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!bot`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/bot)
    : Controls the bot's overall presence (mute/unmute/part).
*   [`!commands`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/commands)
    : Provides a link to the list of commands (which are often tied to modules).

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#parameters)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/module#related-commands)

Twitch

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!next` command (aliased as `!nextsong`) allows anyone in chat to view details about the upcoming song in the StreamElements media request queue. It typically shows the song title, duration, requester, and a link.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/next#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To see the next song in the queue:

    !next

Or using the alias:

    !nextsong

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/next#examples "Direct link to Examples")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

example chat

ViewerName:!next

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:Next song: Epic Sax Guy - 10 Hours \[10h0m0s\] requested by SaxLover https://youtu.be/kxopViU98Xo

example chat

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:There are no songs currently in the queue.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/next#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   This command requires the **Songrequest** module to be enabled and configured in your StreamElements Dashboard (`Chatbot` -> `Modules`).
*   The information displayed depends on the data available from YouTube for the requested track.

    : Provides a link to the full media request queue.
*   [`!songrequest`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/songrequest)
    : Allows users to request songs to add to the queue.
*   [`!skip`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/skip)
    : (Moderator+) Skips the currently playing song.
*   [`!removesong`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/removesong)
    : (Moderator+) Removes a specific song from the queue.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/next#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

# $(teamfighttactics) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(teamfighttactics)` variable - or `$(tft)` - allows you to retrieve and display the current rank and LP (League Points) of a specified Teamfight Tactics player using the StreamElements Chatbot.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use this variable, you need to provide two parameters: the region and the player's Riot ID.

    $(teamfighttactics <region> <Riot ID>)

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    $(teamfighttactics euw styler#euw)$(teamfighttactics na Doublelift#na1)

Example output:

    Current Rank: Gold IV (32 LP)

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Region**: The server region of the player (e.g., `euw`, `na`)
2.  **Riot ID**: The player's unique identifier

Supported Regions[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#supported-regions "Direct link to Supported Regions")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `br` (Brazil)
*   `eune` (Europe Nordic & East)
*   `euw` (Europe West)
*   `jp` (Japan)
*   `kr` (Republic of Korea)
*   `lan` (Latin America North)
*   `las` (Latin America South)
*   `na` (North America)
*   `oce` (Oceania)
*   `pbe` (Public Beta Environment)
*   `ph` (Philippines)
*   `ru` (Russia)
*   `sg` (Singapore)
*   `th` (Thailand)
*   `tw` (Taiwan)
*   `tr` (Turkey)
*   `vn` (Vietnam)

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Why isn't the rank updating immediately?**

A: Rank data may have a slight delay due to API caching. It typically updates within a few minutes after a player's ranked game.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#parameters)
    
*   [Supported Regions](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#supported-regions)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/teamfighttactics#faq)

# Time Variables | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Important: Use IANA Timezones

When using the `$(time.timezone)` variable, always use **IANA Timezone** names. These are standardized identifiers like "America/New\_York" or "Europe/London". Do not use abbreviations like EST or GMT, as they can be ambiguous.

Find the correct IANA Timezone name for your location at [https://nodatime.org/TimeZones](https://nodatime.org/TimeZones)
.

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

StreamElements Chatbot offers two powerful time-related variables:

1.  `$(time.timezone)`: Displays the current time in a specified timezone
2.  `$(time.until)`: Creates a countdown to a specified UTC timestamp

These variables allow you to enhance your stream chat with real-time clock displays and event countdowns.

$(time.timezone)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#timetimezone "Direct link to $(time.timezone)")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#usage "Direct link to Usage")

    $(time.timezone <timezone>)

If no timezone is provided, the variable will return UTC time.

### Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

*   `<timezone>`: (Optional) The desired timezone in IANA format. If omitted, UTC is used.

A list of valid IANA timezones can be found at [Nodatime Timezones](https://nodatime.org/TimeZones)
.

### Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#examples "Direct link to Examples")

1.  Display time in New York:
    
        The current time in New York is $(time.timezone America/New_York)
    
2.  Display UTC time:
    
        The current UTC time is $(time.UTC)
    

$(time.until)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#timeuntil "Direct link to $(time.until)")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#usage-1 "Direct link to Usage")

    $(time.until <timestamp>)

### Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#parameters-1 "Direct link to Parameters")

*   `<timestamp>`: The target UTC timestamp in [ISO 8601](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_8601)
     format.

### Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#examples-1 "Direct link to Examples")

1.  Countdown to a specific time today:
    
        Next stream starts in $(time.until 19:00)
    
2.  Countdown to a future date and time:
    
        Upcoming event in $(time.until 2024-09-20T19:00:00-03:00)
    

Common Use Cases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#common-use-cases "Direct link to Common Use Cases")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Displaying Local Time**: Use `$(time.timezone)` to show the streamer's local time or the time in different viewers' locations.
    
2.  **Event Countdowns**: Use `$(time.until)` to create excitement for upcoming streams, game releases, or special events.
    
3.  **Multi-Timezone Scheduling**: Display multiple timezones simultaneously for international audiences.
    
4.  **Dynamic Stream Information**: Incorporate time variables into stream titles or chat commands to provide real-time updates.
    

Best Practices[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#best-practices "Direct link to Best Practices")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Always use IANA timezone names with `$(time.timezone)` to ensure accuracy and avoid ambiguity.
2.  Use clear and consistent timestamp formats with `$(time.until)` to ensure accuracy.
3.  Consider creating custom commands that combine both variables for comprehensive time information.

Troubleshooting[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#troubleshooting "Direct link to Troubleshooting")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Common Errors[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#common-errors "Direct link to Common Errors")

1.  **Invalid Timezone**:
    
    *   Error message: `unknown time zone lol`
    *   Solution: Double-check the timezone name against the [Nodatime Timezones](https://nodatime.org/TimeZones)
         list. Ensure you're using the full IANA name (e.g., "America/Los\_Angeles" instead of "PST").
2.  **Invalid Timestamp Format**:
    
    *   Error message: `parsing time "19:00:00-03:00" as "2006-01-02T15:04:05Z07:00": cannot parse "19:00:00-03:00" as "2006"`
    *   Solution: Ensure your timestamp follows the ISO 8601 format.

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Can I use these variables in custom commands?**

A: Yes, you can incorporate these time variables into your custom chat commands for added functionality.

**Q: How often do the time variables update?** A: The variables update in real-time with each use, providing current information every time they're called.

**Q: Can I use abbreviations like EST or GMT with $(time.timezone)?**

A: No, always use full IANA timezone names like "America/New\_York" or "Europe/London" to avoid ambiguity and ensure correct time display.

**Q: Can I use these variables to schedule automated messages?**

A: While the variables themselves don't schedule messages, you can use them in combination with StreamElements' scheduling features to create time-based automated messages.

Additional Resources[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/time#additional-resources "Direct link to Additional Resources")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

# $(uptime) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#overview "Direct link to Overview")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(uptime)` variable is a powerful tool in the StreamElements Chatbot that displays the duration of the current stream for a specified user. This feature is particularly useful for viewers who want to know how long a stream has been live.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(uptime)` variable, simply include it in a custom command or message. You can optionally specify a username to check the uptime for a particular streamer.

Syntax: `$(uptime [username])`

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#examples "Direct link to Examples")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Check uptime for the current stream:
    
        !uptimeBot: The stream has been live for 2 hours 15 minutes.
    
2.  Check uptime for a specific streamer:
    
        !uptime shroudBot: shroud's stream has been live for 3 hours 45 minutes.
    

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `username` (optional): The name of the streamer whose uptime you want to check. If omitted, the variable will default to the current stream's uptime.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(game)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game)
    : Displays the current game being played on the stream
*   [`$(title)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title)
    : Shows the current stream title

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Will $(uptime) work for offline channels?** A: No, the `$(uptime)` variable only works for currently live streams. For offline channels, it will typically return an error message "not live".

**Q: Can I customize the uptime format?** A: The default format is "X hours Y minutes". While you can't directly change this format within the variable, you can create custom commands that parse and reformat the output as needed.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#related-commands)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime#faq)

# $(sender) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#overview "Direct link to Overview")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(sender)` variable in StreamElements Chatbot always refers to the user who triggered the command or message. It provides access to various user-related information such as username, loyalty points, ranks, and activity timestamps.

Key Point

`$(sender)` always refers to the command trigger and doesn't accept arguments. If you need to query information about other users, use the [`$(user)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/user)
 variable instead.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`$(source)` can also be used as an alias for `$(sender)`.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(sender)` variable, include it in your chat message or command response using the `$()` syntax. For example, `$(sender)` will display the command trigger's display name.

Available sender Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#available-sender-variables "Direct link to Available sender Variables")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### $(sender)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sender "Direct link to $(sender)")

Displays the message sender's display name.

**Example:**

    Current user: $(sender)

**Output:** `Current user: Styler`

### $(sender.name)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendername "Direct link to $(sender.name)")

Displays the sender's display name in lowercase letters.

**Example:**

    Current user: $(sender.name)

**Output:** `Current user: styler`

### $(sender.points)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderpoints "Direct link to $(sender.points)")

Displays the sender's loyalty currency owned.

**Example:**

    $(sender) has $(sender.points) points

**Output:** `Styler has 100 points`

### $(sender.points\_rank)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderpoints_rank "Direct link to $(sender.points_rank)")

Displays the sender's rank on the loyalty currency leaderboard.

**Example:**

    $(sender) is rank $(sender.points_rank) on the leaderboard

**Output:** `Styler is rank 5/283 on the leaderboard`

### $(sender.points\_alltime\_rank)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderpoints_alltime_rank "Direct link to $(sender.points_alltime_rank)")

Displays the sender's rank on the all-time loyalty currency leaderboard.

**Example:**

    $(sender) is rank $(sender.points_alltime_rank) on the all-time leaderboard

**Output:** `Styler is rank 5/283 on the all-time leaderboard`

### $(sender.level)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlevel "Direct link to $(sender.level)")

Displays the sender's access level.

**Example:**

    $(sender) is level $(sender.level)

**Output:** `Styler is level 2000`

### $(sender.lastmessage)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlastmessage "Direct link to $(sender.lastmessage)")

Displays the sender's last typed message in the chat.

**Example:**

    $(sender) last typed: $(sender.lastmessage)

**Output:** `Styler last typed: !points`

### $(sender.lastseen)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlastseen "Direct link to $(sender.lastseen)")

Displays the time that the sender was most recently seen in the viewer list or chat.

**Example:**

    $(sender) was last seen $(sender.lastseen) ago

**Output:** `Styler was last seen 13m 15s ago`

### $(sender.lastactive)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlastactive "Direct link to $(sender.lastactive)")

Displays the time that the sender most recently typed a message in the chat.

**Example:**

    $(sender) was last active $(sender.lastactive) ago

**Output:** `Styler was last active 13m 15s ago`

### $(sender.time\_online)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendertime_online "Direct link to $(sender.time_online)")

Displays the total time the sender has spent watching the stream.

**Example:**

    $(sender) has been watching the stream for $(sender.time_online)

**Output:** `Styler has been watching the stream for 27m 16s`

### $(sender.time\_online\_rank)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendertime_online_rank "Direct link to $(sender.time_online_rank)")

Displays the sender's rank on the leaderboard for online time watched.

**Example:**

    $(sender) is rank $(sender.time_online_rank) on the online leaderboard

**Output:** `Styler is rank 5/283 on the online leaderboard`

### $(sender.time\_offline\_rank)[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendertime_offline_rank "Direct link to $(sender.time_offline_rank)")

Displays the sender's rank on the leaderboard for offline time watched.

**Example:**

    $(sender) is rank $(sender.time_offline_rank) on the offline leaderboard

**Output:** `Styler is rank 5/283 on the offline leaderboard`

Best Practices[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#best-practices "Direct link to Best Practices")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Use `$(sender)` when you only need information about the command trigger.
2.  If you need to reference other users or allow flexible user queries, use the [`$(user)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/user)
     variable instead.

Troubleshooting[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#troubleshooting "Direct link to Troubleshooting")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   If a variable returns unexpected results, ensure you're using the correct syntax and that the user exists in your channel's database.
*   Remember that `$(sender)` variables don't accept arguments. If you need to query other users, use `$(user)` instead.

Related Documentation[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#related-documentation "Direct link to Related Documentation")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   For querying information about any user, see the [`$(user)` variable documentation](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/user)
    .

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#overview)
    
*   [Aliases](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#aliases)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#usage)
    
*   [Available sender Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#available-sender-variables)
    *   [$(sender)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sender)
        
    *   [$(sender.name)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendername)
        
    *   [$(sender.points)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderpoints)
        
    *   [$(sender.points\_rank)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderpoints_rank)
        
    *   [$(sender.points\_alltime\_rank)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderpoints_alltime_rank)
        
    *   [$(sender.level)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlevel)
        
    *   [$(sender.lastmessage)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlastmessage)
        
    *   [$(sender.lastseen)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlastseen)
        
    *   [$(sender.lastactive)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#senderlastactive)
        
    *   [$(sender.time\_online)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendertime_online)
        
    *   [$(sender.time\_online\_rank)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendertime_online_rank)
        
    *   [$(sender.time\_offline\_rank)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#sendertime_offline_rank)
        
*   [Best Practices](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#best-practices)
    
*   [Troubleshooting](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#troubleshooting)
    
*   [Related Documentation](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender#related-documentation)

# $(twitchemotes) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#overview "Direct link to Overview")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(twitchemotes)` variable is a powerful tool that allows you to display all available Twitch subscriber emotes in your stream chat. This can be useful for showcasing your channel's unique emotes or creating interactive chat experiences.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(twitchemotes)` variable, simply include it in your chatbot command or message. The variable will be replaced with a list of all available Twitch subscriber emotes for your channel.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#examples "Direct link to Examples")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here are two practical examples of how to use the `$(twitchemotes)` variable:

1.  Display all subscriber emotes:

    !emotes Subscriber emotes: $(twitchemotes)

This command will output something like:

    Subscriber emotes: stylerXD, stylerRIP, stylerLOL, stylerHYPE

2.  Create a dynamic emote celebration:

    !celebration Let's celebrate with our awesome emotes! $(twitchemotes)

This command will output something like:

    Let's celebrate with our awesome emotes! stylerXD stylerRIP stylerLOL stylerHYPE

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(twitchemotes)` variable does not accept any parameters. It will always output all available Twitch subscriber emotes for the channel.

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [$(bttvemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/bttvemotes)
    : Lists active BetterTTV emotes in the channel
*   [$(7tvemotes)](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/7tvemotes)
    : Lists active 7TV emotes in the channel

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: Will this variable show emotes from other channels?**

A: No, `$(twitchemotes)` only displays subscriber emotes for the current channel.

**Q: How often is the emote list updated?**

A: The Twitch emote list is cached for 48 hours. To update the list immediately, you can use the command `!emotes reload`.

**Q: Can I customize the output format of the emotes?**

A: The `$(twitchemotes)` variable outputs emotes in a simple comma-separated list. For more advanced formatting, you may need to use custom code.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#related-variables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/twitchemotes#faq)

# !level | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#overview "Direct link to Overview")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!level` command allows streamers and moderators to view or manually set the permission level of a specific user within the StreamElements system. User levels determine access to commands and other features.

While levels like subscriber, VIP, and moderator are often assigned automatically based on platform roles, this command allows manual overrides or assigning custom levels like `Regular` or `Super Moderator`.

**Important:** By default, only users with **Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**To check a user's level:**

    !level <username>

**To set a user's level:**

    !level <username> <level_value>

**To reset a user's level to default (based on their platform role):**

    !level <username> reset

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#examples "Direct link to Examples")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Checking a level:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!level RegularViewer

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, The level of RegularViewer is 100.

**Setting a user to Regular:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!level RegularViewer 300

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Successfully set RegularViewer's level to 300 (Regular).

**Resetting a user's level:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!level RegularViewer reset

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Successfully reset RegularViewer's level to 100 (Everyone).

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<username>` (Required): The exact username of the target user.
*   `<level_value> or reset` (Optional):
    *   Provide a numeric level value to manually set the user's level.
    *   Use the keyword `reset` to remove any manual override and revert to the level determined by their platform role (or default 100 if none).

User Level Values[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#user-level-values "Direct link to User Level Values")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

StreamElements uses the following numeric values for permission levels:

*   `100`: Everyone (Default for non-sub/VIP/mod users)
*   `250`: Subscriber
*   `300`: Regular (Manually assigned via Dashboard or `!level`)
*   `400`: VIP (Twitch only)
*   `500`: Moderator
*   `1000`: Super Moderator (Manually assigned via Dashboard or `!level`)
*   `2000`: Broadcaster

**Note:** Manually setting a level (e.g., setting a non-sub to `250`) grants them the permissions of that level within StreamElements (e.g., access to sub-only commands) but does _not_ grant them platform-specific benefits like sub badges or emotes.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.
*   User levels are fundamental to command permissions configured in the **Chat Commands** section of the Dashboard.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!permit`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/permit)
    : Temporarily grants link permission to a user, often used for users below a certain level.

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

> **What happens if I use the command incorrectly?**
> 
> The bot will guide you. You might see messages like:
> 
> `@User, usage !level USER 500/reset`
> 
> `@User, valid levels are: 100 (Everyone), 250 (Subscriber), 300 (Regular), 400 (VIP), 500 (Moderator), 1000 (Super Moderator)`

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#parameters)
    
*   [User Level Values](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#user-level-values)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#related-commands)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/level#faq)

# !raffle | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#overview "Direct link to Overview")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!raffle` command allows streamers and moderators to create interactive raffles with multiple winners. This feature engages viewers by giving them a chance to win prizes or recognition during the stream.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    !raffle <amount> <duration>

*   `<amount>`: Required. The total reward (pot) for the raffle, distributed among winners.
*   `<duration>`: Required. The duration of the raffle in seconds.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#examples "Direct link to Examples")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Start a raffle with a 100 point reward lasting 60 seconds:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!raffle 100 60

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:The Multi-Raffle for 100 points will end in 60 Seconds. Enter by typing "!join"

**Create a longer raffle with a larger reward:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!raffle 500 180

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:The Multi-Raffle for 500 points will end in 180 Seconds. Enter by typing "!join"

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<amount>` (required): The total reward (pot) for the raffle, which will be distributed among the winners.
*   `<duration>` (required): The duration of the raffle in seconds.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!join`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/join)
    : Used by viewers to enter an active raffle.
*   [`!cancelraffle`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/cancelraffle)
    : Allows moderators to cancel an ongoing raffle.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Moderators can configure raffle settings, such as the maximum number of winners or cooldown period between raffles, through the StreamElements dashboard.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/raffle#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, there are no aliases for the `!raffle` command. However, streamers can create custom aliases through the StreamElements dashboard if desired.

# $(touser) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#overview "Direct link to Overview")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(touser)` variable is a versatile tool in the StreamElements Chatbot that allows you to mention users or display specific words in chat messages. It's particularly useful for creating personalized responses or directing messages to specific users.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(touser)` variable can be used in two ways:

1.  Without input: It displays the name of the user who triggered the command.
2.  With input: It displays the first word provided after the command.

The syntax for using this variable is:

    $(touser)

or

    $(touser) *word*

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#examples "Direct link to Examples")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Example 1: Greeting the command user[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#example-1-greeting-the-command-user "Direct link to Example 1: Greeting the command user")

Command:

    !greet

Response:

    Hello $(touser)! Welcome to the stream!

If user "StreamFan123" uses the command, the output will be:

    Hello StreamFan123! Welcome to the stream!

### Example 2: Mentioning a specific user[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#example-2-mentioning-a-specific-user "Direct link to Example 2: Mentioning a specific user")

Command:

    !shoutout $(touser)

If a moderator types "!shoutout CoolStreamer", the output will be:

    Hey everyone, check out CoolStreamer's channel! They're awesome!

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(touser)` variable accepts one optional parameter:

*   **word**: The first word following the command. If provided, this word will be displayed instead of the command user's name.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(sender)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/sender)
    : Always displays the name of the user who triggered the command.
*   [`$(args)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/args)
    : Displays the first word after the command, or nothing if no word is provided.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`$(touser)` is an alias for `$(1|sender)`, which means it will display the first word after the command if available, or the sender's name if no word is provided.

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: What happens if I use $(touser) with multiple words after it?** A: Only the first word after `$(touser)` will be used. Any additional words will be ignored.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#examples)
    *   [Example 1: Greeting the command user](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#example-1-greeting-the-command-user)
        
    *   [Example 2: Mentioning a specific user](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#example-2-mentioning-a-specific-user)
        
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#parameters)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#related-commands)
    
*   [Aliases](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#aliases)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/touser#faq)

---

# $(title) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#overview "Direct link to Overview")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(title)` variable displays the current title of a Twitch channel. This variable is useful for creating commands that show the stream's title or for integrating the title information into other chatbot responses.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(title)` variable, simply include it in your custom command or message response. The chatbot will replace the variable with the channel's current title when the command is executed.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#examples "Direct link to Examples")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Creating a !title command to display the current stream title:

    !command add !title The current stream title is: $(title)

When a viewer types `!title` in chat, the bot might respond:

    The current stream title is: Playing Spyro! Come join the adventure!

2.  Incorporating the title into a welcome message:

    !command add !welcome Welcome to the stream, $(user)! We're currently $(title). Enjoy your stay!

When a viewer types `!welcome` in chat, the bot might respond:

    Welcome to the stream, ViewerName! We're currently Playing Spyro! Come join the adventure! Enjoy your stay!

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(title)` variable accepts one optional parameter:

*   `username`: The username of the channel whose title you want to check. If not provided, it defaults to the current channel.

Example usage with a parameter:

    $(title OtherStreamer)

This would return the title of the channel "OtherStreamer" instead of the current channel.

Related Variables[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#related-variables "Direct link to Related Variables")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`$(game)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/game)
    : Displays the current game or category of the stream
*   [`$(uptime)`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/uptime)
    : Shows how long the current stream has been live

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Q: How often does the title information update?**

A: The title information is typically updated in real-time, but there might be a slight delay (usually a few seconds) between changing the title on Twitch and the chatbot reflecting the new title.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#parameters)
    
*   [Related Variables](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#related-variables)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/title#faq)

---

# $(weather) Variable | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#overview "Direct link to Overview")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(weather)` variable allows you to display current weather conditions for a specified location in your StreamElements chatbot. It provides comprehensive information including temperature, feels-like temperature, weather description, wind details, humidity, visibility, and air pressure.

warning

Weather data is provided by third-party sources and may not reflect current geopolitical boundaries.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To use the `$(weather)` variable, follow this syntax:

    $(weather "location")

Replace _location_ with the desired city and state/country.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#examples "Direct link to Examples")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Getting weather for New York City:

    $(weather "New York, NY")

Output:

    New York, United States of America: 🌞 27.2 °C (81.0 °F). Feels like 29.5 °C (85.2 °F). Partly cloudy. Wind is blowing from the North at 3.6 km/h (2.2 mp/h). 58% humidity. Visibility: 16 km (9 miles). Air pressure: 1016 hPa.

2.  Getting weather for London, UK:

    $(weather "London, UK")

Output:

    London, United Kingdom: 🌞 13.1 °C (55.6 °F). Feels like 11.7 °C (53.0 °F). Moderate or heavy rain with thunder. Wind is blowing from the West at 13.0 km/h (8.1 mp/h). 88% humidity. Visibility: 7 km (4 miles). Air pressure: 1009 hPa.

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `$(weather)` variable accepts one parameter:

*   `location`: The location for which you want to retrieve weather information. Format as "City, State" for US locations or "City, Country" for international locations.

FAQ[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#faq "Direct link to FAQ")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **How often is the weather data updated?** The weather data is typically updated every 10-15 minutes.
    
2.  **Can I display the temperature in Fahrenheit instead of Celsius?** The variable automatically displays both Celsius and Fahrenheit temperatures.
    
3.  **What happens if I enter an invalid location?** If you enter an invalid or unrecognized location, the chatbot will respond with an error message.
    

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#parameters)
    
*   [FAQ](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/variables/weather#faq)

---

# !nukeusername | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#overview "Direct link to Overview")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!nukeusername` command is a moderation tool allowing moderators to perform bulk actions (timeout or ban) on users whose **usernames** contain specific text or match a regular expression and have chatted within a specified lookback period.

**Warning:** This is a powerful command. Use it with caution, especially with broad match strings or regex, to avoid unintended actions against legitimate users.

**Important:** By default, only users with **Super Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    !nukeusername <lookback_seconds> <action> <match_text_or_regex>

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#examples "Direct link to Examples")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Timeout users for 300s whose username contains "bot123" and chatted in the last 60s:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!nukeusername 60 300 bot123

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Nuked 2 users matching "bot123".

**Ban users whose usernames match a regex pattern (e.g., starts with "troll\_") and chatted in the last 5 mins:**

example chat

![broadcaster badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/5527c58c-fb7d-422d-b71b-f309dcb85cc1/3 "broadcaster")BroadcasterName:!nukeusername 300 ban /^troll\_/i

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Broadcaster, Nuked 1 users matching "/^troll\_/i".

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<lookback_seconds>` (Required): The duration (in seconds, max 300) to scan previous chat messages to find users who chatted.
*   `<action>` (Required): The moderation action:
    *   Number (e.g., `60`): Timeout duration in seconds.
    *   `ban`: Permanently ban the users.
    *   **Note:** Unlike `!nuke`, `delete` is generally not applicable here as it targets message content, not usernames.
*   `<match_text_or_regex>` (Required): The text or pattern to match against usernames.
    *   For plain text matching: `badnamepart`
    *   For regular expression matching: Wrap the pattern in forward slashes, e.g., `/botaccount\d+/i` (the `i` makes it case-insensitive).

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`. It's highly recommended to keep this restricted.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!nuke`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke)
    : Performs similar actions but matches against message content instead of usernames.
*   [`!filesay`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay)
    : Executes commands line-by-line from a text file URL, useful for banning specific lists of users.

Aliases[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#aliases "Direct link to Aliases")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are no default aliases for this command. Custom aliases can be created in the StreamElements dashboard.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#parameters)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#related-commands)
    
*   [Aliases](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername#aliases)

---

# !pause | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#overview "Direct link to Overview")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!pause` command temporarily stops the playback of the current item in the StreamElements media request queue. The queue itself remains intact, and playback can be resumed later.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To pause the currently playing media:

    !pause

**Important:** By default, only users with **Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#examples "Direct link to Examples")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!pause

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Media request playback paused!

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!play`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/play)
    : Resumes media playback after it has been paused.
*   [`!skip`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/skip)
    : Skips the currently playing media item.
*   [`!volume`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/volume)
    : Adjusts the volume of the media player.
*   [`!songrequest`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/songrequest)
    : Adds a song/video to the queue.
*   [`!songqueue`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/songqueue)
    : Provides a link to the media queue page.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#examples)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/pause#related-commands)

# !nuke | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch YouTube Trovo Kick

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#overview "Direct link to Overview")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!nuke` command is a powerful moderation tool allowing moderators to perform bulk actions (timeout, ban, delete) on users whose recent messages contain specific text or match a regular expression.

**Warning:** This is a powerful command. Use it with caution, especially with broad match strings or regex.

**Important:** By default, only users with **Super Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#usage "Direct link to Usage")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    !nuke <lookback_seconds> <action> <match_text_or_regex>

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#examples "Direct link to Examples")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Timeout users saying "spam spam" in the last 60 seconds for 120 seconds:**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!nuke 60 120 spam spam

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Nuked 3 messages matching "spam spam".

**Ban users whose messages matched a regex pattern in the last 5 minutes:**

example chat

![broadcaster badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/5527c58c-fb7d-422d-b71b-f309dcb85cc1/3 "broadcaster")BroadcasterName:!nuke 300 ban /badsite.(com|net)/i

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Broadcaster, Nuked 1 messages matching "/badsite.(com|net)/i".

**Delete messages containing "selling stuff" in the last 30 seconds (Twitch only):**

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!nuke 30 delete selling stuff

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, Nuked 2 messages matching "selling stuff".

Parameters[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#parameters "Direct link to Parameters")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   `<lookback_seconds>` (Required): The duration (in seconds, max 300) to scan previous messages.
*   `<action>` (Required): The moderation action:
    *   Number (e.g., `60`): Timeout duration in seconds.
    *   `ban`: Permanently ban the users.
    *   `delete`: Delete the matching messages (Twitch only, requires Mod status for the bot).
*   `<match_text_or_regex>` (Required): The text to search for.
    *   For plain text matching: `some bad phrase`
    *   For regular expression matching: Wrap the pattern in forward slashes, e.g., `/badword\d+/i` (the `i` makes it case-insensitive).

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`. It's highly recommended to keep this restricted.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!nukeusername`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nukeusername)
    : Performs similar actions but matches against usernames instead of message content.
*   [`!filesay`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/filesay)
    : Executes commands line-by-line from a text file URL, useful for banning specific lists of users.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#examples)
    
*   [Parameters](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#parameters)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/nuke#related-commands)

---

# !openstore | StreamElements Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

On this page

Twitch

Overview[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#overview "Direct link to Overview")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `!openstore` command allows streamers and moderators to quickly re-enable all **regular** (non-sound effect) items in the StreamElements loyalty store that were previously disabled (e.g., using `!closestore`).

Usage[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#usage "Direct link to Usage")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To enable all regular store items, use the following command in chat:

    !openstore

**Important:** By default, only users with **Moderator** permission level or higher can use this command.

Examples[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#examples "Direct link to Examples")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

example chat

![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")ModUser:!openstore

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Moderator, successfully updated 15 items. (Store opened)

example chat

![broadcaster badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/5527c58c-fb7d-422d-b71b-f309dcb85cc1/3 "broadcaster")BroadcasterName:!openstore

![partner badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/d12a2e27-16f6-41d0-ab77-b780518f00a3/3 "partner")![moderator badge](https://static-cdn.jtvnw.net/badges/v1/3267646d-33f0-4b17-b3df-f923a41db1d0/3 "moderator")StreamElements:@Broadcaster, No disabled regular store items found.

Configuration[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#configuration "Direct link to Configuration")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   The command's permission level can be adjusted under `Chatbot` -> `Chat Commands` -> `Default Commands`.

Related Commands[​](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#related-commands "Direct link to Related Commands")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [`!closestore`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/closestore)
    : Disables all _regular_ (non-SFX) items in the loyalty store.
*   [`!disablesfx`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/disablesfx)
    : Disables only sound effect (SFX) items in the loyalty store.
*   [`!enablesfx`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/enablesfx)
    : Enables only sound effect (SFX) items in the loyalty store.
*   [`!redeem`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/redeem)
    : Allows viewers to redeem store items.
*   [`!items`](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/items)
    : Provides a link to the store page.

*   [Overview](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#overview)
    
*   [Usage](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#usage)
    
*   [Examples](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#examples)
    
*   [Configuration](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#configuration)
    
*   [Related Commands](https://docs.streamelements.com/chatbot/commands/default/openstore#related-commands)
